# Big Data in the Age of AI

> Explore the integral relationship between big data and artificial intelligence in this comprehensive course. In this course, Barton Poulson—a professor, consultant, entrepreneur, and data expert—delves into the three Vs of big data: volume, velocity, and variety. Find out how they drive AI advancements. Learn how to handle enormous datasets, use machine learning algorithms, and employ predictive a

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408) | 2h 38m | Beginner | 28K learners
> [Jump to Path Context ↓](#path-context)

### 1. Introduction

#### Big data in the age of AI
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-31649039?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-31649039?u=76281980&t=0)** Several years ago we were deep in the big data revolution when the volume, velocity, and variety of data overwhelmed the systems used to store, manipulate, and analyze it.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-31649039?u=76281980&t=12)** Now we're in the artificial intelligence revolution.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-31649039?u=76281980&t=15)** First predictive AI, then generative AI, and now agentic AI.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-31649039?u=76281980&t=19)** But it's important to remember that big data hasn't gone away and it hasn't become irrelevant.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-31649039?u=76281980&t=25)** Rather, big data has become the new normal.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-31649039?u=76281980&t=28)** It's everywhere, and it's what makes developments like AI possible.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-31649039?u=76281980&t=32)** In this non-technical discussion, we'll look at the ways that you can learn from big data and the technologies that make it possible to find actionable insights in the data that you work with and solve the problems that matter to you.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-31649039?u=76281980&t=45)** I'm Barton Poulsen, and I've been teaching people to use data of all kinds to solve practical problems for over 30 years.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-31649039?u=76281980&t=52)** It is a whole new world, and so let's get started with Big Data in the Age of AI.

### 2. 1. Defining Big Data

#### The volume, velocity, and variety of big data
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] The one thing we know for sure about big data is that, well, it's big.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=5)** I mean, it's really big.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=7)** But you know, what counts as big changes with the times.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=11)** Once upon a time, this set of punch cards, which I believe are for a Jacquard loom, might have been big data.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=20)** Or back in 1969, this was massive.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=23)** This is Margaret Hamilton with the code for the Apollo Guidance Computer.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=26)** She won the Presidential Medal of Freedom in 2016 for this work.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=29)** It was an extraordinary accomplishment and a massive, massive project.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=34)** But what's big at one point in time is normal or even small at another.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=39)** So for example, back in 1992 when I got my first computer, an Apple Macintosh Classic II, it had the optional larger 80 megabyte hard drive.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=49)** I got all the way through grad school on that.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=51)** I wrote my master's thesis, my PhD dissertation on that computer.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=55)** And now, in 2024, I have a relatively modest MacBook Air with two terabytes of internal storage.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=61)** And when I'm at home, it's connected with 10 terabytes of external storage.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=65)** Now, that's 150,000 times as much storage as my first computer.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=71)** So, it's massive by comparison, but it's middling for consumers, and really, it's puny by commercial standards.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=79)** And that gets us to what's called The Three Vs of Big Data or some criteria that are used for defining what counts as big data at a certain point in time.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=90)** The Three Vs are first, volume, and then velocity, and then variety of the dataset.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=98)** And taken together, they constitute big data.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=101)** Now, let me explain each of these in turn.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=104)** First, is volume.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=106)** And really what we're talking about here is when you have more data than fits in your computer's RAM, it's memory.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=111)** You can have more data than fits in a single hard drive.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=115)** So for instance, if you're Facebook and you have data from 3 billion users, or you're Amazon and you have data on 600 million items that you list on your store, you've got a lot of data.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=127)** It can't all fit in one place.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=129)** And so that goes beyond the standard kind of spreadsheet size data sets and gets you to something that requires a different method.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=140)** Or, there's velocity.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=141)** This is where data comes in rapidly and changes frequently.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=146)** Again, going back to Facebook, they get 4 million likes per minute every day of the year.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=152)** Or on YouTube, they get 5 billion videos watched every day.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=157)** And it is changing so fast that you don't have time to sit down and update your dataset manually and then go through the analyses again.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=165)** It needs a different approach.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=168)** Or, variety.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=169)** This is when your data comes in many different formats.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=172)** Think not just one kind of spreadsheet or another, but having videos, or photos, or audio.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=179)** Or, things like GPS coordinators.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=180)** Or, social network connections, which require different kinds of databases to store them.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=185)** All of these are things that go beyond the standard rows and columns of a usual spreadsheet.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=193)** Really, it's data that's hard to manage.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=196)** Some animals are a little more challenging to deal with and have not been domesticated, like zebras.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=201)** And big data is a little like zebras in the data world.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=204)** It's just not easy to work with and it requires very special methods.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=209)** Now, a lot of the methods I'm going to talk about in this course were adapted for big data when it first came out about 10 years ago.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=218)** But things have changed over time.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=220)** And again, what used to be big data in, say, 2014, may fit on your computer these days.
>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=227)** But the problem is that the data that's available has expanded even more so.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=234)** Now, I want to give you a little bit of background and talk about the relative popularity of big data as a search term on Google.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=242)** Here's the last 14 years from 2010 to 2024.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=246)** And you can see that it was really at its highest in the 2016 to maybe 2018 era.
>
> **[4:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=254)** That is when new methods were being developed for handling big data.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=257)** Now, it's tapered down a little over time.
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=260)** You can see a dip around 2021.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=262)** But the important thing is it's not that it's gone away, it's that what was big data has become normal data, and has become the standard operating procedure for so many other tasks and projects in the data world.
>
> **[4:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=278)** You know, it makes me think of the saying that a fish, or, in this case, a seahorse, would be the last one to discover water.
>
> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=284)** That's because it's everywhere.
>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=285)** It's literally the medium that they live and move in.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=289)** The same thing is true of big data in the data world.
>
> **[4:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=293)** Big data is still there.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=295)** It's everywhere. It's all around us.
>
> **[4:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=298)** It has simply become the new normal and it's become what we are working with.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=302)** And so as we go through this course, and I talk about big data, even though that term may not be at the top of your head at each point, it is the foundation of all modern data work.
>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/the-volume-velocity-and-variety-of-big-data?u=76281980&t=316)** And that's something that I'm really excited to talking about and what makes it so relevant, even as we navigate the world of AI, the world of machine learning, and the other things that big data made possible.

#### Machine learning and predictive AI
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/machine-learning-and-predictive-ai?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/machine-learning-and-predictive-ai?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Speaker] When people think about advanced data work these days, their minds are immediately drawn to artificial intelligence and machine learning, the way the mind was automatically drawn to big data and other procedures a few years ago.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/machine-learning-and-predictive-ai?u=76281980&t=14)** But to understand the connection between big data and these other fields, it's worth reminding ourselves about what they all mean.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/machine-learning-and-predictive-ai?u=76281980&t=23)** So to begin with machine learning, well that's a collection of algorithms or computer programs that can find patterns and data to predict outcomes.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/machine-learning-and-predictive-ai?u=76281980&t=32)** And the idea is that those algorithms and prediction will improve over time.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/machine-learning-and-predictive-ai?u=76281980&t=36)** Now, they range from the very simple regression, which in certain cases can be done by hand with a piece of paper and a pencil to the extraordinarily complex, such as deep learning neural networks.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/machine-learning-and-predictive-ai?u=76281980&t=49)** And there are hundreds of other approaches in between those that fall into the general category of algorithms that computers can use to find patterns or ways that the machines can learn from the data.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/machine-learning-and-predictive-ai?u=76281980&t=62)** Now, artificial intelligence generally refers to techniques that allow computers to do things that are typically done by humans, and those programs can show adaptability or intelligence.
>

> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=73)** The biggest difference is that it's goal directed, you get to put down where you want to go.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=78)** And when you interact with the AI, and instead of asking it to help you write code or help you do some kind of research, you tell it what your final goal is, where do you want to get to on that map, and then you let it do the research over multiple steps.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=95)** And at the same time, you give it access and authority to take actions on your behalf.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=101)** And the idea is then it can go through this entire process and reach the goal that you want.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=107)** Now, in terms of describing the process, there are a few different models.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=112)** People use these terms that it talks about perceiving, it's looking around, it's doing the research and reasoning, that's the cognitive elements of it.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=122)** It is taking actions, and then it's learning from the actions or checking and adjusting what it's doing.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=128)** And it's a cycle, it can go through several different times in order to reach the particular goals that you have.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=135)** The big difference here is instead of simply asking it a question, you are now directing it.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=143)** Think of it as like having an intern generative AI might tell you what you need to do.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=149)** It might say, if you're planning a trip, here's some places you could go, here's some things you could do.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=153)** If you are writing some code, it will say, here's some code that you could copy and paste and you could use.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=159)** That's helpful.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=160)** But it is fundamentally taking the role of an advisor in actions that you take.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=166)** On the other hand, with agentic AI, you tell it what you want it to do.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=172)** And you can think of it more like having a very capable intern than just a research assistant.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=179)** Now, the big challenge here is that it requires a lot of trust.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=184)** To get the full element of agentic AI, you're going to do things like give it access to your calendar, and to your e-mail account and actually give it the ability to send emails on your behalf.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=197)** You're going to give it your credit card information and your airline logins and other things.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=202)** And so that requires a substantial amount of trust in the particular agentic AI you're working with.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=208)** You're handing over elements of your life that you want it to take care of.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=213)** So it behooves you to place some limits on it.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=216)** Don't let it go spend a million dollars without asking you.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=220)** Check its progress.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=221)** And of course, as with anything that AI does, verify the results, see what's going on, do a little reality check.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=228)** And then also, as we have with AI, it's going to be important to assess the ethics and the practical implications of the work it does.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=238)** That said, there is enormous process with the growth of agentic AI, that as AI develops, it can take over more and more of the repetitive or automatable tasks to allow us to focus more on the things where we as humans can bring our more distinctive value.
>
> **[4:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/agentic-ai?u=76281980&t=256)** So by partnering with AI, we can actually, in fact, bring out more of that individual value as well.

> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=73)** So think of it as a server that has all the data sets on it.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=77)** Now there are several advantages to data warehouses.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=80)** Number one, the data is typically well structured and curated.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=84)** And it's well structured in part because data warehouses often could only take one kind of data.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=90)** And it would usually be a relational database with the rows and columns of tables.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=96)** And in addition to that, a data warehouse may contain discrete organizational units.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=102)** So for instance, accounting might have their own part of the the warehouse and sales might have their own part of the warehouse.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=110)** This was one way to organize things and these were very popular, say for instance, back in the 70s and 80s.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=117)** But there was a problem and that you ran the risk of ending up with a data dead zone, an abandoned data warehouse.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=126)** The reliance on structured data worked well for a lot of purposes.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=131)** But the explosion of big data brought in enormous amounts of unstructured and semi structured data that didn't fit well in the systems.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=138)** In addition, warehouses sometimes perpetuated the existence of organizational silos or these walls between units that didn't communicate well.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=150)** And truthfully, that undermined some of the promise of the data revolution.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=155)** And so for many organizations, the data warehouse kind of came it solves some problems, but then it seemed to bring along some potential problems of its own.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=164)** That led to the development of our next solution and next metaphor, the data lake.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=171)** This is a data storage that holds data that is structured, and semi structured, and unstructured, any kind of data can go in there.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=182)** And so it's enormously flexible.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=185)** And it's designed to do away with data silos that all of the organization's data from every unit can go in there.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=193)** And so it's potentially available to whoever needs it.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=196)** And really, it's the existence of data lakes through things like Hadoop that made the big data revolution possible.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=205)** But just as with data warehouses, there are some potential risks with data lakes.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=210)** And that is you can end up with a data swamp.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=213)** If the data lake isn't well maintained, if mistakes in the data aren't fixed, if adequate metadata isn't provided, if multiple but different versions of the same data are coexisting, if formats aren't adapted to the software use, you run the risk of getting this swamp like situation, which can be a dangerous place to get lost and really becomes a place where data go to die.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=237)** On the other hand, a more recent hybrid solution known as the lake house, that's a portmanteau of data lake and warehouse, combine some of the advantages of each approach, including the ability to work with both structured and unstructured data with less risk of developing into the swamp.
>
> **[4:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=256)** Then again, that leads us into the most common solution today, which is the cloud.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=261)** The idea here is that a data cloud is something that contains data like a data lake that is is structured, semi-structured and unstructured.
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=269)** So it's very flexible in terms of the content, but it doesn't rely on a local server.
>
> **[4:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=276)** It doesn't rely on local maintenance of the equipment because it's off somewhere else.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=282)** I mean, this is when you use things like Amazon Web Services, better known as AWS or Microsoft Azure or Google Cloud, among others.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=291)** And also because it's fully online, it's more accessible and truthfully, it's more adaptable.
>
> **[4:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=298)** You can get more space immediately, you can get more computing resources immediately as you go.
>
> **[5:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=304)** There's some huge advantages to storing and working with big data in the Cloud.
>
> **[5:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=311)** But as with every other solution, there are some risks and I'm going to call it data dissipation.
>
> **[5:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=318)** The major risks of storing data in the Cloud have to do first with security, where the organization may not be keeping track of who has access to the resources, or it might be susceptible to hacking.
>
> **[5:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=330)** Second, there's cost containment.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=332)** When things are infinitely expandable at any time, you may not be keeping track of the costs that you're racking up.
>
> **[5:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=338)** Third, there's the remote possibility that the services you use might become temporarily inaccessible or they may disappear completely.
>
> **[5:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=346)** You do run the risk of your data dissipating or not knowing what's happening there.
>
> **[5:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=351)** Now, because we are in the Data Cloud era, it's worth pointing out a couple of variations that have become particularly popular.
>
> **[5:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=359)** One is the multi-Cloud, also called Polynimbus.
>
> **[6:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=363)** This is using several different Cloud storage and computing providers simultaneously.
>
> **[6:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=369)** You might use both Microsoft Azure and Google Cloud, and use some IBM Cloud computing resources.
>
> **[6:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=378)** The point here is you actually can integrate them so they're in a single heterogeneous environment.
>
> **[6:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=385)** It's as though they were in a single thing.
>
> **[6:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=388)** Now, that's one popular approach because it lets you use the strengths of each of these providers.
>
> **[6:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=394)** There's also hybrid Cloud.

>
> **[6:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=404)** Think of a local server.
>
> **[6:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=406)** What that lets you do is it lets you keep a lot tighter control on what happens here.
>
> **[6:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-warehouses-data-lakes-and-the-cloud-31649038?u=76281980&t=412)** It's possible also to move back and forth.

#### Edge computing, fog computing, and local computing
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980)

>

>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=11)** For example, in baseball, you can go for the glorious home run, or you can play small ball and just focus on getting runners on base and systematically moving them forward.

>

> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=65)** In big data, this ladder approach goes by a couple of different names.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=70)** One is edge computing.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=72)** And the idea with edge computing is that you have central storage and processing in the regular big data model, and that would be shown by this central unit in the middle of this network.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=83)** And then you have connected devices at the edge of the network.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=88)** But in edge computing, those devices on the edge, the ones on the periphery, can also store and even process data, taking some of the workload away from the central computer.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=104)** Another name for this is fog computing, and this comes from the idea that you have the cloud for data storage and data processing, which is large online servers.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=116)** But fog is the same kind of cloud, but now it's on the ground and it's all around you.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=124)** The idea here is that you're bringing what's in the cloud down to where the people are.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=130)** Now, there are several motivations for this.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=133)** Number one is, when you put things out there on the edge or when you bring the cloud down to where the people are, you can do things much faster.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=141)** You have low latency of response.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=144)** And obviously, if you have poor connectivity, this is a good way of dealing with it, because you don't necessarily have to connect to get the information or to do the processing.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=153)** There can be reduced server load at the central location, but probably one of the most important ones for a lot of consumers is privacy.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=162)** If the identifying or private information never leaves your phone, if it never leaves your watch, if it never leaves your laptop, if it always stays with you, then you don't have the same kind of privacy concerns that might happen when everything's stored in a single central location.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=179)** Now, I can give you a few examples of edge or fog computing that are particularly useful.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=184)** One is facial recognition.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=187)** This can be done on your phone.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=189)** Once a network is trained well enough, it can be done right there on your device.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=196)** Or a more interesting one is sensors in jet engines.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=200)** This is one where the ability to function with low latency and in remote environments is very important.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=206)** Sensors can be tiny.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=208)** And they can actually be inside the jet engine and monitoring temperatures for anomalies to make sure that things are functioning properly as the engine is operating.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=218)** And one of the most science fiction ones is actually putting very small computers, and by very small, I mean 1/3 of a millimeter on each edge.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=229)** That's the thickness of a few sheets of paper.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=231)** These can actually be put inside biological cells, inside cancer cells, and they include a temperature monitor, a power source, and a way of transmitting data.
>
> **[4:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=243)** That is edge computing taken to an extreme.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=246)** In each case, you're taking tasks that maybe could have been done at a large central location, and you're putting them right at the point where they are most needed, where they can be responded to immediately, where it can be done privately, and it can do things that might otherwise be impossible.
>
> **[4:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/edge-computing-fog-computing-and-local-computing?u=76281980&t=263)** And that is the promise of taking some of the tasks of big data and bringing it out of the central location to the edges or out of the cloud, into the fog.

#### Big data for change detection
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Lecturer] Ernest Hemingway, in his book, "The Sun Also Rises," wrote this about change.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=6)** A character was asked, "How did you go bankrupt?"
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=8)** And his response is, "Two ways. Gradually and then suddenly."
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=15)** On the other hand, Charles Darwin talked about change as a very gradual process when he looked at the beaks of finches on the Galapagos Islands.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=24)** And the idea here is speciation.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=27)** That groups change until they become two or more distinct species, whereas previously they were one.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=34)** Now, this happens with living organisms, animals, plants, cellular organisms of all kind.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=40)** It happens with languages.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=41)** They start out being the same language and they diverge into different languages.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=46)** Or it even happens with something like musical styles.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=48)** I mean, go to Wikipedia, see the very, very long articles on the variations of hip hop, as well as heavy metal.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=56)** It's an overwhelming amount of differentiation.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=60)** Now, when you're looking for changes, there are a lot of ways that this shows up in the data world.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=66)** So, for instance, think about something like investing, where you're looking at changes over time.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=71)** This graph shows the last 10 years of data from the S&P 500, one of the major stock market indices in the US.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=79)** You can see there's a dip in the middle when the pandemic hit in 2021.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=84)** And you can see another broader dip in '22, '23.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=88)** But the general pattern is clear, it goes up over time.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=91)** It's tripled in value over 10 years.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=94)** In fact, if I'd been able to show you more than 10 years of data, the pattern is even more obvious.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=99)** This is the source of what's called buy-and-hold investing.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=103)** You buy a stock that you expect to do well over the long term, and you just hold onto it, so you don't move.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=111)** Now the question is, is this pattern reliable and should you buy something and hold onto it even when there are these big dips?
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=118)** Well, there are two general risks with change and trying to find change or ignoring change.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=125)** Number one is missed opportunities.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=127)** If there is, in fact, a genuine change in the market or the environment you're dealing with and you don't react to it, you might miss a change in market conditions, audience dynamics, something that could potentially bring value to the work that you do.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=142)** On the other hand, the flip side of that is being overreactive, and that's the risk of making expensive, unnecessary changes.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=149)** Reactive investing leads to people buying when stocks are high, selling when stocks are low, and losing money in the overall.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=157)** And so you can think of these as both the false negatives and the false positives in trying to identify change.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=166)** Now, there are a lot of different ways that change can show up.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=170)** Number one, in a static space, just thinking, plotting data in a two-dimensional or three-dimensional, or any-dimensional space.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=178)** You can look at bi-variate outliers, you can look at multi-variate outliers.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=182)** You can look at points that don't cluster, using whatever algorithm you're using.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=186)** Those could be meaningful but misunderstood clusters, or it could be some sort of random fluctuation in the data.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=195)** A similar thing happens with time series, where you're looking at changes over time for one or more variables.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=201)** You can see spikes and dips, and you can also see glitches where something obviously went wrong with the recording mechanism.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=208)** You can then try to smooth out trends based on means, or quartiles, or some other value, and look at the general pattern, ignoring the moment-to-moment fluctuations.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=220)** Both approaches can be valid.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=223)** The problem is you sometimes end up dealing with unpredictable points.
>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=227)** They're in the dataset, and maybe they happen more than once, but you don't have an explanation and you're not able to build a model, at least not using standard methods, to capture the variation of that idiosyncratic point or group of points.
>
> **[4:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=243)** And this is where big data comes to the rescue.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=247)** Now, big data, among other things, is big, and what it allows you is more detail.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=253)** You can stick things under the microscope.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=257)** Big data gives you more patterns that you can see, and in greater detail.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=262)** You can zoom way in, and still have the resolution you need to do effective modeling.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=267)** I mean, there are more cases.
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=269)** There are more variables, perhaps over a greater span of time.
>
> **[4:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=274)** It gives you a lot to work with.
>
> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=275)** That's why it's called big data.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=279)** One result of this is that even small fluctuations or even small variations in clustering become detectable, not necessarily actionable, not always, but they are detectable.
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=290)** You can see some potential thing there in the data you can act on.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=295)** Big data makes that possible.
>
> **[4:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=298)** It also makes it possible to do kinds of validation that are not available elsewhere.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=302)** Large data sets facilitate the validation of findings.
>
> **[5:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=308)** So for instance, if you've got a large dataset, when you're building your model, when you're training your model, you can use cross validation.
>
> **[5:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=315)** Chop your dataset up into 9, 10, 15 different groups, and try to model the patterns for each one.
>
> **[5:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=324)** That's cross validation when you are developing your model.
>
> **[5:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=327)** Once you have a model, you can have another group holdout that you never use for developing your model.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=332)** And you can test your model on them.
>
> **[5:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=334)** Now, this is very common procedure in machine learning and data science, and places where you have large data sets.
>
> **[5:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=343)** It is not common procedure in other fields like mine, which is experimental social psychology, where data sets are measured in one or 200 cases.
>
> **[5:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=353)** You simply don't have enough data to allow these kinds of validation.
>
> **[5:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=357)** Instead, you have to rely on the hope that you designed your study perfectly and that whatever results you get are meaningful.
>
> **[6:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=367)** You can see that the validation approaches that come from big data allow you to get past just those I-hope-I-did-it-right mechanisms.
>
> **[6:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-for-change-detection?u=76281980&t=376)** And that is really one of the best ways to find reliable, potentially meaningful and potentially actionable insights, anomalies, or quirks, or new groups in your data that you and the people you're working with can do something meaningful with.
