#### Big data as proxy data
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Now, this may seem a little odd in the context of a course on big data where we're trying to find ways to benefit from the enormous quantities of data that are now available, but I'm actually a huge fan of taking the three Rs that we know so well from the physical world, reduce, reuse and recycle, and applying them in the data world too.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=22)** Now, there's a couple of reasons for that.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=23)** Number one is, there are costs to gathering data.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=27)** Whether you're doing a survey with pencil and paper, whether you're doing in-person interviews or online, please-give-us-your-feedback things, it takes time, it takes money, and really you're drawing on the time that your respondents have, that's a limited resource, and their goodwill, another limited resource.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=47)** And so there are always costs to gathering data.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=52)** Second, there are costs of preparing data.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=54)** There's the common truism that in a data science project, 80% of your time is spent preparing the data for analysis, and the remaining 20 is spent on analyzing it, or interpreting it, or doing other things.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=66)** If there were some way to reduce the costs of gathering data and the costs of preparing data, and in fact, have them approach zero, wouldn't that be a fabulous thing?
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=77)** Well, it turns out that is possible.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=79)** Now, number one, you do have the option of gathering passive data.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=83)** Anytime somebody gets on a social media platform or an e-commerce site, there is data gathered of some kind, and a little information about where they're located, what device they were using, how long they were there.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=96)** And so there is that passive data.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=98)** It's not very difficult for the respondents to provide 'cause they maybe don't even know they're providing it, although it does take a toll on the goodwill of people once they find out that their data has been used.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=110)** But there is passive data.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=113)** A second one is archival data.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=115)** Data that people have gathered previously and is available.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=118)** Maybe it's in a clean format, maybe it's not, maybe it needs to be prepared in a different way, but there's a lot of data out there, maybe in your organization, maybe in open data portals, something you can use that doesn't require you to reinvent the wheel to get the data for your project.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=138)** And there's a related method of meta-analysis.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=141)** This is where you take the results of several published studies, and without ever even having the raw data, but looking at the results that they posted, their summary statistics, you can then combine them into a larger-scale result along with modeling some of the things about each study that might push their results one way or another.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=163)** In the social sciences, my field, this is a wonderful approach.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=166)** In the medical sciences, it is also taken as one of the gold standards for getting a composite finding across large numbers of studies.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=175)** So all three of these are great ways of using data that doesn't have so much cost in terms of gathering or in terms of preparing.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=185)** It's something that is easy to get or it's already there.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=188)** And it allows you to reuse existing data, recycle it in new ways, and get some insights.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=195)** On the other hand, over the last couple of years, with the advent of generally available generative AI, one other interesting possibility has come up, and that is the ability to generate proxy data from generative AI.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=211)** Literally, this is where you're telling your large language model, "Tell me how people would respond to these questions," or, "Tell me how people would respond under these different situations."
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=221)** So it's simulated data, but it turns out that it's got a couple of huge advantages.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=226)** Number one, it can give you really detailed data.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=228)** Generative AI methods are trained on data from nearly everywhere and nearly everyone.
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=235)** It's got a range that you will never be able to match on your own.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=240)** It's got data on subgroups and changes over time.
>
> **[4:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=243)** It's got the level you need to put things under the microscope.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=247)** Also, it allows you to assess effects.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=250)** There are many different ways of asking the large language model, the generative AI, "How would people respond to this question?"
>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=258)** or more interestingly, "How would they respond to this question if I gave them different prompts?"
>
> **[4:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=263)** That's doing an experiment.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=265)** And one of the interesting things about this is researchers have found that the AI predictions about how people would respond under these different conditions is often more accurate than what you get from expert human forecasters.
>
> **[4:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=280)** Now, if you're familiar with missing data methods, you might know about multiple imputation as a way of creating distributions for missing data.
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=290)** Think of this as an absolutely completely supercharged version of missing imputation.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=295)** Now, it's not sufficient, it's not enough to say I've made a finding, because it's all simulated, but what this approach is really good for is finding promising leads for human data.
>
> **[5:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=309)** You get to find that this prompt has a bigger potential effect than this prompt, when you're doing a survey, people will respond differently to this than to this.
>
> **[5:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-as-proxy-data?u=76281980&t=318)** Once you've been able to narrow down some of the most promising methods from the least promising methods, that allows you to save time when it comes to gathering new data, it gives you promising leads for that human data, and those leads are more likely to lead to identifiable and actionable insights.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **CLI Commands:** find (3)
> **Code Keywords:** require (1), this. (1)
> **Definitions:** is a  (1)
> **Speakers:** - [instructor] (1)


### 4. 3. Ethics in Big Data

#### Big data and privacy
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Most tech companies would think that their wildest dreams had all come true if they could bring in $5 billion of revenue.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=10)** But to lose $5 billion because you didn't adequately protect people's privacy, well, that would be about your worst nightmare.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=18)** And that's something that Facebook gets to deal with at this exact moment because of a landmark fine for violating the privacy requirements of the European Union's General Data Protection Regulation, or GDPR.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=31)** Now, the European Union's GDPR, which has been in force as of May of 2018, makes some important restrictions.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=38)** It puts limits on data.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=40)** Not all data that is accessible, data that you can see online, or that you can get from people by asking them, can be legally used.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=48)** For instance, you may ask for people's phone numbers to enable two-factor authentication, but you can only use the phone number for that purpose.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=57)** You can't use it for audience targeting or segmentation.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=62)** Also, there's a dramatically-changing landscape when it comes to privacy.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=66)** The laws and regulations are evolving rapidly and the interpretations of these regulations.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=72)** So we are seeing how the GDPR gets interpreted and how it plays out.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=77)** And then there's things like the California Consumer Privacy Act, which will be enforced in 2020, rephrase, which will be enforced in 2020, shares many of the same elements as the GDPR and many states, and most countries, have their own versions of privacy regulations, which unfortunately don't always mesh.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=96)** And so it makes working in an international environment, which is what people on the internet do, a little more challenging.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=104)** Now, if you want to know specifically what kind of information is considered private by these regulations, here's an answer.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=113)** Demographic data that indicates racial or ethnic origin, political opinions, religious or philosophical beliefs, trade union membership, genetic data, biometric data for the purpose of uniquely identifying a natural person, data concerning health, or data concerning a natural person's sex life or sexual orientation, as well as things like web behavior and IP addresses.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=132)** That's a huge amount of information that, once upon a time, would've been part of the free for all for internet marketing.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=139)** But now that information is restricted, and this list, by the way, is from Article 9 of the GDPR.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=144)** Well, what can you do?
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=147)** There are a few major things that are going to help you get started on proper privacy.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=154)** So for instance, the GDPR requires explicit affirmative consent to gather personal data.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=161)** People have to check the box to say yes, and it can't already be checked.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=165)** It has to be blank, and they have to check it, and they have to give you permission to gather personal data.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=171)** But in the process, you have to justify the collection.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=174)** You have to explain how that data is collected, for what purposes, how it's going to be processed.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=181)** And then really a critical one here is that the customers control the data.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=185)** The customers can download all of the data that you collect on them.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=189)** If they think that there's an error, they can correct it, and you have to make the revisions.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=193)** And they can ask you to completely delete all of their information from your records.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=198)** So these are the sorts of things that might fall under common sense civil rights or human rights on the internet, but they are things that had to be codified in the GDPR, and they are now part of the legal and regulatory landscape.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=213)** Now, it does bring up another question.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=216)** We have a lot of kinds of information that are not allowed, but how close do you have to be to those things?
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=223)** We have what you might call the minimal or the minimalist interpretation.
>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=227)** And the idea here is that only variables that directly record personal characteristics are blocked.
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=233)** So you would have to have a variable or a field that says race or ethnicity or religion, and it would have to be an answer to that direct question.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=242)** And so the minimal version says, well, only if you ask that specific question.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=247)** The problem is that nearly all variables on everything are correlated with these kinds of personal characteristics.
>
> **[4:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=255)** It's not difficult to infer a person's race, or religion, or education, or so many other things by, for instance, the websites they visit.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=265)** And so it turns out that the minimal approach, which only looks at direct questions, is ineffective protection because all of these protective categories can be inferred through other processes.
>
> **[4:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=277)** Then there's what you might call the maximal approach, and that is that all variables that are even correlated with personal characteristics are blocked and can't be used in targeting audiences and marketing.
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=290)** Well, this approach basically removes all of the data.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=294)** Everything is out.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=296)** And the problem is that that maximalist approach makes modeling, that is creating statistical models to provide the services that your company's designed to do, it makes that nearly impossible.
>
> **[5:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=307)** And so again, it's not a workable solution.
>
> **[5:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=311)** So obviously, you're going to have to find some kind of balance between those two extremes.
>
> **[5:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=317)** It's going to have to depend on, among other things, the field that you're working in, the kind of data that you have available to you, and of course your local laws and regulations.
>
> **[5:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=327)** And if you want more information about some of these challenges and some potential solutions, we have another course available, AI Accountability Essential Training, which will be a great introduction to these topics for anybody working in big data, data science, machine learning, and artificial intelligence.
>
> **[5:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/big-data-and-privacy?u=76281980&t=344)** That way you can start doing your work and you can do it in a way that is productive, that is useful, that provides something of value for your clients and your customers, without running afoul of the laws, the regulations, and the social practices that you're dealing with.

#### Intellectual property, corporate data, and generative AI
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] Big data doesn't get any bigger than the data that goes into training generative AI.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=6)** In a sense, each company that develops a model is using some industrial commercial vacuum to suck up all the data that they possibly can.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=16)** As I've mentioned elsewhere, a large amount of the data comes from sources like Common Crawl and RefinedWeb.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=21)** Those are both publicly accessible data sets for building AI models.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=26)** On the other hand, other people have suggested that prominent AI models have included sources like YouTube, Reddit, Twitter, textbooks, and a lot of other things floating around on the internet.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=37)** As you might guess, this has led sometimes to lawsuits with claims of intellectual property or IP violations where the work of artists, authors, and news sources has been repeated verbatim in the output of a generative AI model, it's hard to deny that you got past a paywall when you're showing the same words.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=57)** Now, unfortunately, this has not been resolved in the US and one of the things we can find is that in other countries around the world, laws vary.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=69)** Different countries have enacted different policies when it comes to data, intellectual property, and generative AI.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=75)** So for example, in some countries, all data is available for generative AI regardless of whether it was copyrighted or behind a paywall or what have you.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=85)** Obviously, these are very big differences from one place to another, and at the moment, those are still open questions that have not been resolved definitively at a local level or at a global level.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=101)** Separately from that, there's a situation where the data that you upload to a generative AI program, so you give it a document to look at or your interactions, the back and forth that you have with it, those could become incorporated into the training data and potentially used to create responses for other people, which is probably not what you had in mind.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=124)** Now, there's a few things you can do about that.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=127)** Number one is be careful about sharing personal data if you don't want it to get out there and become part of other people's work.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=137)** Think twice about whether you include the content of your diary or something else.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=142)** There's also the issue of corporate data.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=144)** Many organizations have issued really strict policies that nothing that is considered private corporate data should ever be uploaded to an AI because it becomes unclear what's going to happen with it.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=159)** There are solutions to this and that is that certain models or certain versions of models come with a guarantee to not share your data, and so it's going to be on you to figure out exactly which ones have the level of confidentiality, of privacy and protection that you want.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=180)** Then there's a third one where there's really no good way of getting around it, and that is when people upload unlicensed data.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=187)** So if somebody is able to get past a paywall, say they have a subscription to a new site that otherwise is not publicly available, you have to pay to get it, and they upload that article, well, that's one way that the information can get there, and that is just not ever supposed to happen.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=204)** And so it becomes a major responsibility for people to make sure that anything they do put in the machine is in fact, something that they are allowed to share, that they have the rights to share, as well as checking whether the particular AI that they're using is going to guard things as private and confidential, or whether there's a possibility that it will get sucked into a larger model.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=229)** Really, there's no solid answer at this point in time in late 2024, except to say, exercise caution.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=239)** Be careful which models you're using.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=242)** If you are concerned about privacy, about confidentiality, make sure to choose a model that includes guarantees of those.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/intellectual-property-corporate-data-and-generative-ai?u=76281980&t=250)** Otherwise, handle it with care and be aware that for the benefits you're getting from an AI, there are certain risks that come along with them.

#### Environmental impact of big data and AI
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/environmental-impact-of-big-data-and-ai-31644610?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/environmental-impact-of-big-data-and-ai-31644610?u=76281980&t=15)** Now the energy and the resources go into two main things.

>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/environmental-impact-of-big-data-and-ai-31644610?u=76281980&t=35)** ensembles working nonstop to develop the algorithms behind the AI programs, and

>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/environmental-impact-of-big-data-and-ai-31644610?u=76281980&t=56)** And this also takes a phenomenal amount of energy.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/environmental-impact-of-big-data-and-ai-31644610?u=76281980&t=59)** It's why a number of organizations are trying to build their AI plant right by rivers or dams to try to get both energy and water both at once.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/environmental-impact-of-big-data-and-ai-31644610?u=76281980&t=71)** And really, if you want to put all of this into perspective, consider this.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/environmental-impact-of-big-data-and-ai-31644610?u=76281980&t=76)** entered a deal in September of 24 to reopen the Three Mile Island nuclear power plant and buy all of the energy from that recommissioned power plant for 20 years.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/environmental-impact-of-big-data-and-ai-31644610?u=76281980&t=86)** That's a phenomenal amount of energy that is necessary for using in generative and agentic AI.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/environmental-impact-of-big-data-and-ai-31644610?u=76281980&t=94)** To give you a good idea of what this really all works to, think about Microsoft has entered a deal to reopen Three Mile Island.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/environmental-impact-of-big-data-and-ai-31644610?u=76281980&t=105)** that's the nuclear reactor in Pennsylvania in the US that had a partial meltdown in 1979.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/environmental-impact-of-big-data-and-ai-31644610?u=76281980&t=112)** Now, technically, Microsoft isn't going to own it, Constellation Energy will be the owner, but Microsoft entered a deal in September of 2024 to buy all of the energy from the recommissioned power plant for 20 years, primarily to power generative AI.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/environmental-impact-of-big-data-and-ai-31644610?u=76281980&t=129)** That's extraordinary.

>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/environmental-impact-of-big-data-and-ai-31644610?u=76281980&t=212)** And just to keep in mind, it's one thing if there were only one major AI model out there, but there's tons.

>

> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/environmental-impact-of-big-data-and-ai-31644610?u=76281980&t=238)** This right here is a microcontroller, think something like a Raspberry Pi.

>

>

>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=81)** Second, the issue of privacy.

>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=89)** And now there's a long standing practice of one organization collecting data and selling it to another and so on and so forth.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=97)** And that's why some of these organizations know so much about you.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=101)** But the idea is that data needs to be private, especially things that have personally identifiable information, especially things about your health records and your financial records, that those need to be private.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=114)** And then the third one is about algorithmic decisions.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=116)** If a machine learning algorithm, say, for instance, you're applying for a loan on your phone, and you enter your information, you give it access to your credit report, and then it makes a decision.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=128)** Now, if you get approved, fabulous.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=131)** But if you get denied for a loan or a mortgage or a job or something else, that's a decision that impacts you in a negative way.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=139)** And you need to be able to understand what happened there and potentially contest the decision.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=146)** So these three principles about big data, data collection and privacy and being able to understand and potentially contest algorithmic decisions have been part of the data world for a few years.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=158)** And some of the best known regulations about this concern the General Data Protection Regulation, or the GDPR that was founded in the European Union in 2018.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=169)** So it's been over six years that that's available, and it's had a significant impact.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=175)** Other countries outside of the EU, the UK has their own version of the GDPR.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=180)** Many other countries have variations on the laws.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=185)** And we have entire courses that talk in more detail about these principles.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=190)** So I want to go past those ones right now and get more specifically to laws for AI and especially generative AI.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=199)** And now ChatGPT, the most well known and most commonly used version of generative AI was released in the end of November of 2022.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=209)** So it's really important to look at laws that came in after that time, because they are going to specifically address issues of generative AI.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=218)** The first thing I wanted to talk about is trust.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=221)** And the laws that affect trust, which come in, either at a country level, or a continental level, or even a state level, they address things like, you shouldn't be using AI to trick people.
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=235)** So many places have bans on what are called deep fakes or making it look like one person is somebody else or making it sound like a person is saying something that they didn't or a video showing something that didn't happen.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=248)** Now, one way to get around this is several organizations require that whenever you have AI generated material, a photo, a video, a text, whatever, it has to be labeled as such.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=259)** And deliberately misleading people with deep fakes can be a violation of applicable laws.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=267)** The second one is safety.
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=269)** And you can think about the oath that doctors take first do no harm the Hippocratic Oath.
>
> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=275)** Well, there's a lot of ways that AI could do harm, and we're going to try to avoid those.
>
> **[4:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=280)** And a lot of the regulations having to do this, ask for human centric system.
>
> **[4:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=287)** So it says put people first and look out for people's well-being primarily try to bake it in as well as you can.
>
> **[4:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=292)** And they'll place special restrictions on high risk applications.
>
> **[4:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=297)** Now, obviously, that includes military, but it can include a lot of other things like banking and finance, it can include a city's or country's infrastructure, their transportation systems, their power, good, their utilities, and so on.
>
> **[5:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=311)** Everything that's connected to the internet, and everything that runs digitally is potentially at risk.
>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=316)** And that's why AI can be very clever.
>
> **[5:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=319)** and people get very concerned about the potential for bad actors using AI to trip up these systems.
>
> **[5:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=325)** And that's why there have been a range of regulations, not just at the country level, but at larger levels to address these.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=332)** There's also the potential for AI to have a measurable significant impact on a country's or locale's economy, tanking a stock market system, shutting down its trading, locking out banking machines, any number of things can happen.
>
> **[5:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=348)** and so there are very potential risks that come in these large-scale sectors, and regulations have been developed to address those.
>
> **[5:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=357)** The third area I want to mention is accountability, and this is very similar to the one with big data.
>
> **[6:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=364)** The idea is if you apply for a loan and you get denied, or if somebody uses an algorithm in making a sentencing decision about whether somebody gets parole or how long they're going to go to jail, there needs to be accountability for that decision.
>
> **[6:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=377)** You can't just point to the computer and said, he said it.
>
> **[6:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=381)** Instead, the systems, according to many of these laws must be understandable and traceable.
>
> **[6:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=387)** That is tricky because generative AI in particular, is not understandable and traceable.
>
> **[6:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=394)** It works in mysterious ways.
>
> **[6:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=395)** And that's true about deep learning neural networks, which are often used with big data as well.
>
> **[6:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=401)** Now, the picture I have here is a flowchart of yes, no decisions at many levels.
>
> **[6:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=405)** That is definitely not a deep learning neural network or how generative AI works.
>
> **[6:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=411)** But there are situations in which simple flowcharts just yes, no things have been shown to be approximately as effective as neural networks, while being infinitely more understandable, and easy to interpret and easy to troubleshoot.
>
> **[7:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=427)** Many laws also ask for independent oversight over algorithms.
>
> **[7:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=432)** So not asking the developers to police themselves, but having other organizations that are in charge of auditing, checking how well these things work.
>
> **[7:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=441)** And another one is the question of liability, who's responsible if something goes wrong?
>
> **[7:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=446)** Well, most laws say both developers and users can be liable for misuse.
>
> **[7:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=452)** And so nobody gets to say it wasn't me, it was them.
>
> **[7:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=455)** Everybody has some role in keeping things responsible and under control.
>
> **[7:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=460)** Now, in terms of global AI legislation, probably the most significant is the European Union's Artificial Intelligence Act of 2024.
>
> **[7:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=470)** But there are similar ones, the Council of Europe, there are measures in China and Dubai, the African Union and Brazil.
>
> **[7:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=478)** The United States has had proposals for nationwide regulations, but those are still in flux and remains to be determined how that will play out within the United States.
>
> **[8:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=489)** Now, these are not all of the regulations, there are some of the big ones, there are a lot of others that are being developed.
>
> **[8:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=495)** And of course, the problem is, AI is a newly developing field is growing explosively.
>
> **[8:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=501)** And so things will be changing quickly over time.
>
> **[8:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/laws-affecting-big-data-and-ai-31631657?u=76281980&t=504)** If you work in the field, you're going to want to spend extra attention trying to understand how the legal framework is changing and what's going to affect you because, among other things, you want to be able to do great things with your AI, but you want to make sure that you also are able to stay in bounds and work effectively at all times.

> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=211)** If it happens to an entire server, you've got an extraordinarily huge problem.

> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=215)** Is the code that's used to process and analyze the data, is the code complete and is it functional?
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=222)** And you have to worry about whether, for instance, the code has updated between now and then, which is why, for instance, it's common practice to include the usable copies of the packages that you use when you're doing the programming.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=237)** So, those update a lot.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=238)** This way you always have the version that you know worked.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=242)** And then, are the relations intact?
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=244)** And by that I mean the connections between the different tables in your data.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=249)** You have to have a way of referring between them to make a complete data set.
>
> **[4:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=254)** Are those still valid?
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=257)** And then finally, there is the issue of security.
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=260)** Are the data and the code safe from hackers?
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=262)** Remember, data's enormously valuable, and it's a target for anybody who's looking to get a little bit of extra stuff for free.
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=271)** Or in a big data project, because there's so many people involved, you have to be sure that the data and the code are safe from accidental changes by unauthorized users.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=282)** I think about, for instance, just my genealogical data.
>
> **[4:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=286)** I log in there, somebody's made a change, they went back to the same wrong thing that got corrected and you got this big problem.
>
> **[4:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=293)** Think about what happens on Wikipedia, the little editing wars.
>
> **[4:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=297)** But people sometimes log in, and if they have access, they might make a change without realizing how much impact they're having on other major projects.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=306)** And then, the last one, to get back to our Fortran issue, are they future-proof?
>
> **[5:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=312)** Can you store the data?
>
> **[5:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=314)** Can you store the code in such a way that you know it will be usable at least a few years from now?
>
> **[5:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=320)** Maybe not forever, but at least a few years.
>
> **[5:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=323)** So for instance, if possible, don't store your data in a proprietary format, which requires a license and requires the company that made it to update things.
>
> **[5:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=334)** If possible, store it in an open format.
>
> **[5:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=337)** You know, CSV files are nice.
>
> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=339)** They don't keep the metadata so you have other options for that, but something that you know will be around for at least a few years.
>
> **[5:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=346)** That way you can guarantee at least the short term longevity of your data.
>
> **[5:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=351)** And the whole thing makes it easier to manage and to govern the data that is used in your data science projects over time.
>
> **[5:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-governance?u=76281980&t=359)** So, you can get both more insight, more meaning, and, truthfully, more value out of your project.

#### Batch processing vs. stream processing
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Jazz music is inseparably connected with improvisation.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=5)** With a small combo, it's possible to have just the outlines of the tune and then create the whole thing on the go.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=12)** When it works well, it can be an extraordinary experience.

>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=34)** There's an analogy between this, between improvisation and composition in music and in data.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=42)** In jazz, the improvisation, the coming up in the stream of the moment versus the composition where the work has to be done ahead of time and you got to put a bow on it before you move on, that's a lot like in data, what is called stream processing, where you're processing the data as it comes in, live in real time, versus batch processing, where you take data that's been wrapped up and put a bow on it, it's in a data set, it's set, and you run with it.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=72)** Now, let's take a quick look at this.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=74)** Batch processing is data at rest, meaning it's static, it's stationary.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=82)** Now, I'm not trying to talk it down.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=84)** This is the kind of data that I work with.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=86)** It's data that's in a data set, and it's what it is, and you can analyze that data in as much detail as you desire.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=95)** You have time to go back and forth with it.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=98)** You can look for patterns, you can find groups, you can make predictions based on rather sophisticated and time-consuming models.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=106)** All of those are possibilities with standard batch data.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=109)** Create the data, put it together, say it's done, then do the analysis and do your work.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=116)** Compare that to stream.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=118)** Instead of having your baskets of apples and they're now on a conveyor belt, you may not even keep the old data.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=123)** Maybe you just have a window of data that you're saving, because maybe you're just looking for changes over a short period of time, or you're looking for significant anomalies that might, for instance, trigger a problem with the system, a potential breakdown with a machine, an attempt at fraud, as something that triggers the next actions that result from your analysis.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=144)** Now, I do want to make one important distinction.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=147)** Everybody likes to have an organization that operates efficiently and responds well to changing situations.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=153)** That's one reason why agile development and management are so popular.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=158)** And so there may be an automatic preference for a data approach that seems speedy and responsive, and maybe agile too.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=167)** But the thing to remember is that stream processing isn't better.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=170)** It's not a new and improved version of batch processing.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=173)** It's a different process.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=177)** Streaming data and streaming analysis often relies on the different infrastructure.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=181)** You use different kinds of storage systems, you have different kinds of databases.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=185)** You have different ways of incorporating the data.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=188)** It often uses different methods.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=190)** You can't do an elaborate neural network on streaming data.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=194)** You often have to simplify the model depending on the kind of data and the volume that you have coming in.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=201)** And most significantly, stream processing has different goals than batch processing.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=207)** Again, stream processing is designed to look for very quick trends or immediate anomalies, something that requires immediate action, something where the business simply can't survive without that moment-to-moment responsiveness.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=220)** Batch processing is designed to allow you to look at things in more depth, and that is the traditional method of working with data.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=229)** And so my point here is simply to tell you that these two approaches exist.
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=233)** There are two different paths, and depending on the purposes of your organization, you'll want one or the other.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=241)** But generally, it's important to remember that they serve different goals, use different methods, and so it's a decision that you need to consult with the people on your data science team.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/batch-processing-vs-stream-processing?u=76281980&t=250)** And when you're doing your big data projects, you need to think about it carefully and see how well that matches up with the goals of your organization.

>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/distributed-storage-and-processing?u=76281980&t=59)** And for that reason, Hadoop became synonymous with big data.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/distributed-storage-and-processing?u=76281980&t=64)** Major conferences were named the Hadoop Conference, and people used it as a way of symbolizing big data.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/distributed-storage-and-processing?u=76281980&t=72)** Now, what it did is it allowed you to spread the same dataset across many, many different computers.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/distributed-storage-and-processing?u=76281980&t=76)** It could take care of the redundancy.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/distributed-storage-and-processing?u=76281980&t=78)** It could take care of the fault problems.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/distributed-storage-and-processing?u=76281980&t=80)** It could do an amazing number of things, but it was built for local storage, and it wasn't built for processing.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/distributed-storage-and-processing?u=76281980&t=88)** And so Hadoop, while it initiated the big data age through the distributed storage and certain kinds of distributed processing, it really was a foundation and not the ultimate solution.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/distributed-storage-and-processing?u=76281980&t=102)** So for instance, right now we're in the age of cloud services.

>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/distributed-storage-and-processing?u=76281980&t=126)** And if you create an app that runs on big data, you can have what's called a multi-platform container.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/distributed-storage-and-processing?u=76281980&t=133)** So something like Docker, which is a Linux container engine that allows you to create the app that, like the containers on a container ship, you load 'em in what you want there.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/distributed-storage-and-processing?u=76281980&t=144)** It's super flexible, load it on whatever boat, get it out of there, it moves.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/distributed-storage-and-processing?u=76281980&t=148)** Containers allow you to create these big data applications and run them on basically any kind of architecture.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/distributed-storage-and-processing?u=76281980&t=156)** It's one of the amazing developments and the progression of distributed development, distributed processing, and finding a way of getting the insights from big data out to your customers.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/distributed-storage-and-processing?u=76281980&t=171)** So we've progressed from Hadoop to cloud to containers, and who knows what's going to come next, which is of course why I want to take the next video to talk about ways of preparing for an uncertain and unknown future in the big data world.

>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/an-evolving-data-landscape?u=76281980&t=226)** But no matter what you do, remember to focus on your goals.

>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/an-evolving-data-landscape?u=76281980&t=237)** It's there to help us get useful insights to actually know what to do to solve a particular problem.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/an-evolving-data-landscape?u=76281980&t=245)** And the new hardware, the new software, the new methods, are nothing more than tools to help you reach those goals.
>
> **[4:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/an-evolving-data-landscape?u=76281980&t=254)** So focus on your goals and let those be the guiding factor in your decisions about whether to include new technologies, how to integrate them into your workflow, and how you can get value out of them.
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/an-evolving-data-landscape?u=76281980&t=269)** Now, one really important thing, in case it's not completely obvious, is that because of the changing environment, there is a critical need for continual training and support, not just for the tech people, but for everybody in your organization to better understand how they can use data and big data to inform their own decisions and how they can get the value out of it.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/an-evolving-data-landscape?u=76281980&t=294)** And for instance, managers need to know what kinds of decisions can be answered, what kind of support they need to give to the people who will be doing the technical work on a daily basis, and how salespeople can integrate that into the work that they're doing.
>
> **[5:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/an-evolving-data-landscape?u=76281980&t=309)** The training and support is necessary any time you have a competitive and rapidly involving environment, which is absolutely the case with big data.
>
> **[5:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/an-evolving-data-landscape?u=76281980&t=319)** Remember, it's the constant building up, step by step, that's going to help both you and your organization, not just to stay in step with everybody as you go from big data to machine learning to AI, but really to get to that great next step, to get that breakthrough, to get that insight, and possibly to get that competitive advantage that motivated you to embrace big data in the first place.
