### 6. 5. Analyzing Big Data

#### Challenges with data preparation
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Salmon can be farmed or they can be caught wild.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=4)** But either way, it takes a fair amount of work before they're turned into this.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=9)** Everybody knows that food prep is an important, although time consuming and frequently tedious, part of cooking, there's a similar principle in any big data project.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=21)** The rule of thumb is that about 80% of the time on a big data project is spent preparing the data.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=28)** And that's been my own experience.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=30)** Now, there are several reasons why this may be the case.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=36)** It includes things like, how is the data entered?
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=40)** If you're using wild caught data, meaning data that you found out there in the world and that maybe was entered with free text, you have to look at things like place names.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=49)** Here are four different ways of indicating California.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=52)** You can write it out, you can use various abbreviations.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=55)** And the inclusion of a period, at least by default, marks it as a separate answer than the one without a period.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=64)** Or when people are putting in dates, here are four different ways of writing the same dates.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=68)** Now, humans looking at these know that they refer to the same thing, but a computer will read them by default as different things.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=76)** And you have to do a little bit of cleanup work to make sure that the dates are all read the same way and formatted the same way.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=83)** Or phone numbers, again, the same phone number in four different ways.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=89)** You know, for instance, that if you have these in a spreadsheet, they're going to sort separately, but you can reformat them so it knows that they're all phone numbers.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=96)** It does them appropriately, and it's this kind of cleanup work, this becomes an important part of getting things ready for your big data project.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=104)** Then there are other issues like units of measurement.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=108)** If you ask for somebody's weight and they put 150 or 68 or 10.7, well 150 is pounds, 68 kilograms is the same weight and 10.7 stone if you're dealing with somebody from the United Kingdom, that also has 150 pounds.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=125)** So several different ways of measuring these.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=128)** And we all know about examples where, for instance, NASA has not adequately converted from one unit to another, and space probes have crashed as a result of that.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=138)** Then there are errors.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=139)** If a person puts in 2.7 children, that's not possible.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=142)** You can't have fractional children.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=144)** You can have an average that's fractional, or 270 children too many or negative 27.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=150)** You can't have a negative number on a counted value like this.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=156)** And then of course, missing data.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=158)** In some data sets, an eight might indicate a missing value and -999 might indicate a missing or a period or a simply.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=166)** And there are different kinds of missingness, you can have not a number, not available, missing completely at random.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=173)** All of them mean different things.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=175)** And when you're preparing your data, you have to go through these and be thorough in getting them all in the same format, with the same meaning and interpretation all the way through.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=186)** And of course, that's to say nothing of the amount of processing required for dealing with unstructured data like cell phone videos.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=193)** And it gets to an interesting question, where's the return on investment and where's the balance point?
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=198)** Should you clean wild data?
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=200)** Or should you gather new data that is in the structure and with the encodings that you want?
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=209)** So for instance, here's a microscope image of cancer cells.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=213)** And if you're dealing things like health records, the project can be a nightmare, which is why companies like for instance, Recursion Pharmaceuticals, who do drug development, where they try to find applications of existing drugs to orphan diseases, they figured out that it was cheaper, faster, and easier to develop their own technology, to gather and analyze data from half a million experiments per week, with a goal of soon hitting a million per week.
>
> **[4:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=243)** They figured out this would be the most cost effective and research informative method of gathering data to get it.
>
> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=251)** They did the math and realized that gathering their own data with their own proprietary methods, so they could then feed it into their algorithms for analyzing the data would be the best way to reach their goals as opposed to trying to clean the wild caught data.
>
> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=266)** And so it becomes a trade off.
>
> **[4:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=268)** And depending on your exact circumstances, you might be able to use the wild data.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=273)** You may need to gather new custom bespoke data, but no matter how you decide to go about it, you do need to give yourself adequate time for the demanding work of preparing data in your big data project.
>
> **[4:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=288)** Remember the 80/20 rule, again, about 80% of the time on a project is spent getting ready for it, 20% for analysis.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/challenges-with-data-preparation?u=76281980&t=296)** You can find ways to facilitate that, to streamline that and get to the meaning and the insight that you're looking for faster and more efficiently.

>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=69)** Now, in terms of how you frame things, it's important to remember who is making and implementing the final decision.
>

>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=104)** And in that case, visualization is going to be critical to get the value out of your big data project.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=112)** Remember, humans are visual animals, and you get much higher bandwidth with graphics.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=117)** A picture is after all worth a thousand words.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=122)** And so let me make a few recommendations for your graphics in a big data project or anywhere.
>

>

>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=137)** Make it no simpler.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=138)** You want to make it as clear as possible to focus on the data and not get distracted by other things going on in the graphics.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=146)** Second, it's a really good idea to provide a method to give detail as needed.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=151)** Let them click on things, drill down, get some of the source data, get additional context.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=157)** That gives richness to a graphic, especially one that is initially rather simple.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=163)** And then to state the obvious, provide labels for your axes, what's on the X, what's on the Y, what are the different groups, and give the sources for your data so the meaning of it is complete.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=175)** And then there are a few things to be cautious about.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=179)** First, be cautious of 3D graphics.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=181)** Now there's one kind, which is the false third dimension like you see right here where you have bars that have depth.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=188)** There's basically no reason to ever do that.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=191)** The other one is a 3D graphic like a 3D scatter plot.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=194)** It's really cool as long as it's moving, but as soon as it stops, it's very difficult to read, and I personally never use them and I recommend that people avoid them unless there is some really compelling reason to include it.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=207)** Another one that's a little contentious is the issue of interactivity, not just with VR goggles, but really putting radio buttons and sliders on your graphics.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=216)** The risk is this, people will get distracted by the interactivity, and they'll just start playing with it, spinning around your graph and clicking on things to see what happens.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=225)** At that point, the interface has taken attention away from the data itself, and that's a delicate balance, something you need to think about carefully.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=234)** Closely related to that is the use of novel graphs like this one.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=238)** They're cool, they're pretty, they attract attention.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=241)** They are often very hard to read and hard to read well enough to know what to do about it.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=248)** Now, that doesn't mean don't use them.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=250)** It means be very careful and thoughtful when you think about using a novel kind of graph.
>
> **[4:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=256)** Truthfully, in terms of the best ROI or return on investment or the best value, the most information from a graphic, it's going to be really simple ones.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=267)** Bar charts, histograms, line charts, and scatter plots will probably get you 90, 95% of the value you need from data visualization, even on a large, big data project.
>
> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=284)** It doesn't matter that the data set is massive or that the data set gets involved.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=289)** By the time you're getting it down, the simplification to the level that is needed by the decision makers to use it in a productive way, these kinds of graphs will probably give you the kind of insight you need without distracting people from the meaning of the data.
>
> **[5:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/visualizing-big-data?u=76281980&t=307)** And that is the main purpose of visualization in any big data project.

#### Data mining
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Back several generations in my family tree, I have some ancestors who were miners.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=5)** They would go down to work in the mines early Monday morning and wouldn't come back up until Saturday night.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=11)** It was backbreaking and lung-blackening work that I'm grateful I would never have to do.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=18)** But to be perfectly clear, that's not what we're talking about when we're talking about data mining.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=23)** Rather, data mining is the practice of working with large data sets to find potentially valuable insight.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=32)** Think of it this way.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=33)** Computer algorithms, especially deep learning neural networks, are able to go through millions of images and automatically identify all of the pictures with cats in them and show you where the cats are.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=44)** They draw the frame around them.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=46)** Data mining's a little like that, but instead of finding cats, maybe you're trying to find new customers or new treatments for diseases or students with exceptional potential, really, anything that's important to you using the same general concept.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=65)** The idea is pretty simple.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=66)** You get a lot of data in your computer, millions of cases and maybe thousands of variables.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=74)** And you have the algorithm start looking for patterns of some kind in the data.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=79)** Now, there is one major risk in doing all this, and that is what I personally call baseball stats.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=86)** That's not to be confused with the real data of baseball, but you get things like this.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=92)** The batter's a career three-for-three against left-handed relief pitchers on interleague play before the eighth inning on away games when the team is leading by at least four runs after the All-Star break.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=101)** And you got to wonder how the batter's even been up to bat three times.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=104)** This is capitalizing on chance.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=106)** These are such small numbers that these are meaningless patterns, even if they give people something to talk about.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=113)** The major challenge in data mining is to find patterns, but not get these kinds of false positives.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=120)** And in fact, it is false positives that are one of the major risks.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=125)** That's if somebody rolls a 12 with two dice, that might mean something if it's a good outcome.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=130)** And if they do it again, you might suddenly think they know how to roll a 12.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=134)** Well, that's not really the case, because what you're not doing is adequately account for the role of chance.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=140)** Lots of things can happen at random.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=142)** A person can flip 10 heads in a row.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=144)** It doesn't happen very often, but there's a known probability for that.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=148)** And it's important to always know what is the normal variation and maybe slightly beyond that to say, "This is normal."
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=156)** And when you start looking at many, many possible effects, that becomes critical.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=161)** And that's one reason any time you do a data mining project, you especially need to be careful about doing verification.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=167)** That's the double-checking, that's seeing if your pattern holds up in a different dataset.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=173)** That's why it's common in data science to break up your original dataset into what's called a training dataset and a testing or validation dataset, to control for these tendencies towards false positives.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=187)** But if you can do that, there's some great insights you can get out of data mining.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=191)** For instance, you can find new market segments, groups of people whose interests have not been adequately addressed before.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=198)** You've got another niche there, something you can do.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=202)** You can also look for new kinds of product and market match, especially when it turns out that a product can be used in unexpected, novel ways.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=212)** There are things like market basket analysis where you can say that any time a person buys this and this, there's an increased probability they will also buy this.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=219)** So, if you're doing e-commerce, you show them that extra item online or you give them an incentive to buy it.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=225)** And then, there's a whole separate category of time series mining, where you're looking for events that happen over time, or the closely-related sequence mining where you're not saying when they happen, just that it happened before this and after that.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=241)** Both of those can be enormously useful in predicting trends with the interactions you have with businesses or customers.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=250)** Now, if you'd like more information on this, we have another course called Data Science Foundations Data Mining, which gives you some concrete examples of how each of these kinds of analyses can be worked and how the results can be interpreted and put into effect.
>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=264)** But the basic idea here is the same.
>
> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/data-mining?u=76281980&t=266)** When you've got data and when you've got a lot of data, you've have something that potentially has great value if you know how to go through it and mine through it and find those patterns that you and your organization can act on.

#### Sentiment analysis
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980)

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The best thing anybody's ever said about the videos I make is that they were better than bacon.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=7)** Now I took that as a huge compliment, and if you're in business or interacting with people in some way, then you know it's usually a good idea to know how things are going over with people.
>

>

>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=129)** Any one of these makes the task more difficult, not impossible, just more difficult.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=135)** There are also variations in spelling and grammar, as I talked about in text analytics, you need to account for these variations in spelling and realize that those are fundamentally the same thing that they're talking about.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=147)** Then there's the use of irony and sarcasm where the written literal meaning is often opposite of the intended meaning, and you have to have a way of compensating for that, especially if irony and sarcasm account for a substantial portion of your data.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=164)** And then there is the issue of non-text data in sentiment analysis, you may go, what does that mean?
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=171)** The most obvious one is emojis as evaluative data.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=176)** So each of these emojis, which come up in reviews, come up on social media posts, they tell you something about how the person feels about what you've said or about the product or the service you offer.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=188)** Now the nice thing is each of these emojis has code beneath it that lets you know what it is.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=194)** And you can then treat that largely the same way you treat text.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=197)** But then you can start looking at things like memes that people post.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=201)** If it's about your product, your service, your company, then those become an important part of evaluating the affective or emotional inclinations toward you as well.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=212)** And then beyond that, you can actually use sentiment analysis as a form of added value in other projects.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=219)** Just a few days ago, the SentiMATE chess algorithm, which was developed by researchers at University College in London, they found a way to do sentiment analysis to train AI that plays chess.
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=233)** Specifically, they looked at critics' evaluations of recorded chess games, and they're looking for evaluative terms, things like brilliant or ingenious or foolish or stupid.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=247)** Then they use those critiques of chess play to reinforce the chess playing algorithm.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=253)** So that sentiment becomes a guiding principle in setting up their machine learning and artificial intelligence to guide them in the development of their product.
>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=264)** And this is something that can be adapted in so many different circumstances where you take that affective label, that sentiment, and then you use that to guide your analysis and guide your implementations.
>
> **[4:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/sentiment-analysis?u=76281980&t=277)** Anything you can do to find more value and ways to better meet the needs of the people you're serving is going to be a huge advantage for your own organization.

#### Retrieval-augmented generation (RAG)
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=0)** Encyclopedias have been around for a long time, going back hundreds or even thousands of years, and while everybody who has worked on encyclopedias has made monumental efforts to be as accurate and as comprehensive as possible at that time, it's kind of amusing to look at early versions that, for instance, predate space travel or television or automobiles or have totally different national boundaries than what currently exists.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=28)** It turns out that a lot of information has a pretty short shelf life.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=33)** AI has similar limits and it's a little bit like a warehouse.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=37)** The warehouse may be enormous, but it's still a single building in a single place.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=43)** In a similar way, generative AI models, because they are very expensive and very time-consuming to train, to make them work in the first place.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=52)** you know, you can't just make a new one every time something happens.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=57)** Consequently, most of the large generative AI models are limited to the range of information included.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=64)** Now it's a very broad range, but it's not the stuff sitting in your filing cabinets or your particular company's policies.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=72)** It's a lot of stuff, but it's not everything.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=74)** Also, it's limited by cutoff dates by the information they had available to the model when they were training it.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=82)** And as a result, it tends to give general and bounded responses, it'll say, based on my general understanding of this, and based on the information available to me at the time, I can tell you this, there is one other issue with generative AI that people know well, and that is that they can hallucinate, they can make things up and make it sound very persuasive.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=105)** And so these are some of the common limits of generative AI.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=109)** And there are some important developments that help get around some of these limitations.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=115)** In getting past these limits, I want to talk about retrieval augmented generation or rag.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=123)** And it goes beyond these things.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=125)** And it does it in a couple of different ways.
>

>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=129)** So it augments the information that is available to the large generative model with up to date information.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=137)** And it can use in house data.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=139)** So things from your filing cabinets, you can use your policies, your customer data, your interactions, your social media sources.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=148)** And also when it does that it is able to cite the sources and it can also specifically limit itself to those sources.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=156)** And that kind of focus and a form of accountability makes a very big difference.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=162)** So it can do things like go to products that your company has and look up the product specifications from your own data.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=171)** It can look at policies, it can find and quote relevant policies about reimbursement or travel, or expenses from your own policies.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=182)** And if you're in the research world, if you're doing legal research or medical research, you can have it search case law, you can have a search medical journals, and give you the citations to the exact paragraphs and the sources that it's using, you can limit it to your own internal information, if needed.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=200)** This makes it much more usable in a lot of situations.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=204)** Now, a lot of people would say, well, that's just because you're giving a bad prompts, you just need to know how to engineer your prompts better.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=212)** No, it's it's much more than better prompts.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=216)** It is a fundamentally evolutionary approach.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=221)** I mean, think about it this way, there's a three-step loop.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=224)** The first thing it does is it retrieves the information, it finds the source documents that are available in your particular knowledge base.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=234)** Second, it reads those it examines the data and pulls the most relevant passages from the specific documents that you've asked it to rely on.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=244)** And then third, it generates, it'll write a response, it'll produce an answer that is grounded in those specific sources that you have asked it to rely on.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=253)** This makes it a much more focused, much more relevant way of using generative AI in applied settings.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=261)** And, you know, what that means is it uses your documents and it gives sources and that does a lot to both limit the risk of hallucinations and maximize the applicability and the reliability of the data in your situations.
>
> **[4:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/retrieval-augmented-generation-rag?u=76281980&t=276)** That really realizes the practical promise of generative AI, making it directly relevant to the 99.9% of companies that are not AI developers, but who can directly benefit from the potential offered by generative AI, but in ways that are more circumscribed, more directly focused on their applications and more trustworthy.

#### Using big data to make small data
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/using-big-data-to-make-small-data?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/using-big-data-to-make-small-data?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Host] One of the great paradoxes of big data is that sometimes all of the technological wizardry, all the equipment, all the huge amount of effort that goes into it is put into motion to help with something as theoretically simple as choosing whether to go left or right at the fork in the road.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/using-big-data-to-make-small-data?u=76281980&t=19)** The idea here is that big data is frequently used to create small data, the small amount of information, the direction, the couple of restaurant recommendations that the end user wants.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/using-big-data-to-make-small-data?u=76281980&t=34)** It's really another example of the general principle that all analysis, all data analysis is an act of simplification.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/using-big-data-to-make-small-data?u=76281980&t=43)** You are taking something very complex, something potentially huge and overwhelming and reducing it with hopefully still maintaining the general form and feel to something that is more usable and actionable.

>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/using-big-data-to-make-small-data?u=76281980&t=113)** Do they like to be on the freeway?

> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/using-big-data-to-make-small-data?u=76281980&t=115)** So they want the scenic route or they want to avoid tolls?

> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/using-big-data-to-make-small-data?u=76281980&t=118)** And you can also bring in data from other travelers to identify potential slow downs or detours in the road.
>

>

> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/big-data-in-the-age-of-ai-24512408/using-big-data-to-make-small-data?u=76281980&t=139)** That is big data being put into the best possible use for an application with consumer orientation or take something like a job search, which can be a very time consuming, stressful, unpleasant experience.
